					<h1 id="section_0">Kroger</h1>
					<div class="tagline"></div>

				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kroger_Co.&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Kroger Co.">Kroger Co.</a>)</span></div>
			</div>
			
			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><p class="mw-empty-elt">


</p>
<p><b>The Kroger Company</b>, or simply <b>Kroger</b>, is an American <a href="/wiki/Retail" title="Retail">retail</a> company founded by <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Kroger" title="Bernard Kroger">Bernard Kroger</a> in 1883 in <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati" title="Cincinnati">Cincinnati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a>. It is the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>' largest <a href="/wiki/Supermarket" title="Supermarket">supermarket</a> by revenue ($121.16 billion for fiscal year 2019),<sup id="cite_ref-stores.org_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stores.org-4">[4]</a></sup> the second-largest general retailer (behind <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-stores.org_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stores.org-4">[4]</a></sup> Kroger is also the <a href="/wiki/Retail#Global_top_ten_retailers" title="Retail">fifth-largest retailer in the world</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_employers_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="List of largest employers in the United States">fourth largest American-owned private employer in the United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Kroger is ranked #20 on the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> rankings of the largest United States corporations by total revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><caption class="fn org">The Kroger Company</caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" class="logo" href="http://www.kroger.com">www<wbr></wbr>.kroger<wbr></wbr>.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table><p>As of 2 February 2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kroger&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Kroger operates, either directly or through its subsidiaries, 2,757 supermarkets and multi-department stores.<sup id="cite_ref-ourbusiness_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ourbusiness-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-opera_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opera-7">[7]</a></sup> Kroger's headquarters are in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Cincinnati" title="Downtown Cincinnati">downtown Cincinnati</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10K_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10K-8">[8]</a></sup> It maintains markets in 35 states and the <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">District of Columbia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-opera_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opera-7">[7]</a></sup> with store formats that include <a href="/wiki/Hypermarkets" class="mw-redirect" title="Hypermarkets">hypermarkets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Supermarket" title="Supermarket">supermarkets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Big-box_store" title="Big-box store">superstores</a>, <a href="/wiki/Department_store" title="Department store">department stores</a>, and 242 <a href="/wiki/Jewelry" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewelry">jewelry</a> stores (782 <a href="/wiki/Convenience_store" title="Convenience store">convenience stores</a> were sold to EG Group in 2018).<sup id="cite_ref-ourbusiness_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ourbusiness-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-opera_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opera-7">[7]</a></sup> Kroger-branded grocery stores are located in the Midwestern and Southern United States.  Kroger operates 35 food processing or manufacturing facilities, 1,567 supermarket fuel centers, 2,270 pharmacies and 221 The Little Clinic in-store medical clinics.<sup id="cite_ref-ourbusiness_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ourbusiness-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-opera_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opera-7">[7]</a></sup></p><p>Kroger's employees are mostly unionized <a href="/wiki/Collective_bargaining_agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Collective bargaining agreement">collective bargaining agreements</a> and many are represented by the <a href="/wiki/United_Food_and_Commercial_Workers" title="United Food and Commercial Workers">United Food and Commercial Workers</a> (UFCW).<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none"><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Beginning">Beginning</span></h3>
<p>In 1883, <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Kroger" title="Bernard Kroger">Bernard Kroger</a>, the fifth of ten children of <a href="/wiki/German_Americans" title="German Americans">German immigrants</a>, invested his life savings of $372 to open a grocery store at 66 Pearl Street in downtown Cincinnati. The son of a merchant, he ran his business with a simple motto: “Be particular. Never sell anything you would not want yourself.”<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup>   He experimented with making his own products, such as turtles, so that customers would not need to go to a separate farm.
</p><p>In 1884 Kroger opened his second store. By 1902, the Kroger Grocery and Baking Company had been incorporated. By this time, the company had grown to forty stores and sold $1.75 million worth of merchandise each year. In addition, Kroger became the first grocery chain to have its own bakery.<sup id="cite_ref-ohiohistorycentral.org_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohiohistorycentral.org-12">[12]</a></sup></p><p>In 1916 Kroger company began self-service shopping. Before this all articles were kept behind counters, and customers would ask for them, and then clerks would deliver them to customers.<sup id="cite_ref-ohiohistorycentral.org_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohiohistorycentral.org-12">[12]</a></sup></p><p>In 1929, it was rumored that <a href="/wiki/Safeway_Inc." title="Safeway Inc.">Safeway</a> would merge with Kroger.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p><p>In the 1930s, Kroger became the first grocery chain to monitor product quality and to test foods offered to customers, and also the first to have a store surrounded on all four sides by <a href="/wiki/Parking_lot" title="Parking lot">parking lots</a>.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="1950s.E2.80.931960s"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1950s–1960s">1950s–1960s</span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r923042769/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:left;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption-center{text-align:center;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Kroger_logo_(1939%E2%80%9361).svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Kroger_logo_%281939%E2%80%9361%29.svg/200px-Kroger_logo_%281939%E2%80%9361%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="145" data-file-width="192" data-file-height="139"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 200px;height: 145px;" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Kroger_logo_%281939%E2%80%9361%29.svg/300px-Kroger_logo_%281939%E2%80%9361%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Kroger_logo_%281939%E2%80%9361%29.svg/400px-Kroger_logo_%281939%E2%80%9361%29.svg.png 2x"> </span></a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Kroger_logo_(1961-2019).svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Kroger_logo_%281961-2019%29.svg/200px-Kroger_logo_%281961-2019%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="165" data-file-width="375" data-file-height="309"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 200px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Kroger_logo_%281961-2019%29.svg/200px-Kroger_logo_%281961-2019%29.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="200" data-height="165" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Kroger_logo_%281961-2019%29.svg/300px-Kroger_logo_%281961-2019%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Kroger_logo_%281961-2019%29.svg/400px-Kroger_logo_%281961-2019%29.svg.png 2x"> </span></a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="thumbcaption" style="background-color:transparent">Earlier variants of the Kroger logo, including one used from 1939-1961 (<i>top</i>), and the previous variant, 1961-2019, still extant on Kroger brand products (<i>bottom</i>)</div></div></div></div>
<p>Beginning in 1955, Kroger began acquiring supermarket chains again, expanding into new markets. In May, Kroger entered the <a href="/wiki/Houston,_Texas" class="mw-redirect" title="Houston, Texas">Houston, Texas</a>, market by acquiring the Houston-based 26-store chain <a href="/wiki/Henke_%26_Pillot" title="Henke &amp; Pillot">Henke &amp; Pillot</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> In June, Kroger acquired the Krambo Food Stores, Inc. of <a href="/wiki/Appleton,_Wisconsin" title="Appleton, Wisconsin">Appleton, Wisconsin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> In late July, it purchased Child's Food Stores, Inc. of <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_Texas" title="Jacksonville, Texas">Jacksonville, Texas</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In January 1956, the company bought out Big Chian Stores, Inc., a chain of seven stores based in <a href="/wiki/Shreveport,_Louisiana" title="Shreveport, Louisiana">Shreveport, Louisiana</a>, later combining it with the Childs group. All of these chains adopted the Kroger banner in 1966.
</p><p>During all the acquisitions, in September 1957, Kroger sold off its <a href="/wiki/Wichita,_Kansas" title="Wichita, Kansas">Wichita, Kansas</a>, store division, then consisting of 16 stores, to <a href="/wiki/Dillons" title="Dillons">J. S. Dillon and Sons Stores Company</a>, then headed by Ray S. Dillon, son of the company founder.
</p><p>In October 1963, Kroger acquired the 56-store chain Market Basket, providing them with a foothold in the lucrative southern California market. (Prior to this time Kroger had no stores west of Kansas.)
</p><p>Kroger opened stores in Florida under the SupeRx and Florida Choice banners from the 1960s until 1988, when the chain decided to exit the state and sold all of its stores; <a href="/wiki/Sweetbay_Supermarket" title="Sweetbay Supermarket">Kash n' Karry</a> bought the largest share.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="1970s">1970s</span></h3>
<p>In the 1970s, Kroger became the first grocer in the United States to test an electronic scanner and the first to formalize consumer research.
</p><p>Although Kroger has long operated stores in the <a href="/wiki/Huntsville,_Alabama" title="Huntsville, Alabama">Huntsville</a>-<a href="/wiki/Decatur,_Alabama" title="Decatur, Alabama">Decatur</a> area of northern <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">Alabama</a> (as a southern extension of its <a href="/wiki/Nashville,_Tennessee" title="Nashville, Tennessee">Nashville, Tennessee</a>, region), it has not operated in the state's largest market, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham,_Alabama" title="Birmingham, Alabama">Birmingham</a>, since the early 1970s, when it exited as a result of intense competition from <a href="/wiki/Winn-Dixie" title="Winn-Dixie">Winn-Dixie</a> and local chains <a href="/wiki/Bruno%27s_Supermarkets" class="mw-redirect" title="Bruno's Supermarkets">Bruno's Supermarkets</a> and Western Supermarkets.
</p><p>Kroger built an ultra-modern dairy plant (Crossroad Farms Dairy) in Indianapolis in 1972, which was then considered the largest dairy plant in the world.
</p><p>Kroger exited the Chicagoland area market in 1970 selling its distribution warehouse in Northlake, Il. and 24 stores to the Dominick's Finer Foods grocery chain. 
</p><p>Kroger exited Milwaukee in 1972, selling a few stores to <a href="/wiki/Jewel_Food_Stores" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewel Food Stores">Jewel</a>. Kroger would later return in 2015 upon its acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Roundy%27s" title="Roundy's">Roundy's</a>.
</p><p>Kroger entered the <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte</a> market in 1977 and expanded rapidly throughout the 1980s when it bought some stores from <a href="/wiki/BI-LO_(United_States)" title="BI-LO (United States)">BI-LO</a>. However, most stores were in less desirable neighborhoods and did not fit in with Kroger's upscale image. Less than three months after BI-LO pulled out, that company decided to re-enter the Charlotte market, and in 1988, Kroger announced it was pulling out of the Charlotte market and put its stores up for sale. <a href="/wiki/Ahold" title="Ahold">Ahold</a> bought Kroger's remaining stores in the Charlotte area and converted them to BI-LO.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="1980s">1980s</span></h3>
<p>Kroger had a number of stores in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Pennsylvania" title="Western Pennsylvania">Western Pennsylvania</a> region, encompassing <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a> and surrounding areas from 1928 until 1984 when the U.S. began experiencing a severe economic <a href="/wiki/Early_1980s_recession" title="Early 1980s recession">recession</a>. The recession had two significant and related effects on Kroger's operations in the region. One of them was that the highly cyclical manufacturing-based economy of the region <a href="/wiki/Steel_crisis" title="Steel crisis">declined in greater proportion than the rest of the U.S.</a>, which undercut demand for the higher-end products and services offered by Kroger. The second effect of the economic recession was to worsen labor-management relations, causing a protracted labor strike in 1983 and 1984. During the strike, Kroger withdrew all of its stores from the Western Pennsylvania market, including some recently opened "superstores" and "greenhouses", selling these stores to Wetterau (now part of <a href="/wiki/SuperValu_(United_States)" title="SuperValu (United States)">SuperValu</a>), who promptly <a href="/wiki/Flipping" title="Flipping">flipped</a> the stores to independent owners while continuing to supply them under the <a href="/wiki/FoodLand" title="FoodLand">FoodLand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shop_%27n_Save_(Pittsburgh)" title="Shop 'n Save (Pittsburgh)">Shop 'n Save</a> brands.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Kroger's exit ceded the market to lower-cost, locally owned rivals, most notably <a href="/wiki/Giant_Eagle" title="Giant Eagle">Giant Eagle</a> and the SuperValu-supplied grocers. (Kroger purchased Eagle Grocery company, whose founders went on to create Giant Eagle.) Kroger still maintains a presence in the nearby <a href="/wiki/Morgantown,_West_Virginia" title="Morgantown, West Virginia">Morgantown, West Virginia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wheeling,_West_Virginia" title="Wheeling, West Virginia">Wheeling, West Virginia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Weirton,_West_Virginia" title="Weirton, West Virginia">Weirton, West Virginia</a>/<a href="/wiki/Steubenville,_Ohio" title="Steubenville, Ohio">Steubenville, Ohio</a>, areas where Giant Eagle has a much smaller presence and the SuperValu-supplied stores are virtually nonexistent, though in all of these cases, Walmart remains a major competitor and <a href="/wiki/Aldi" title="Aldi">Aldi</a> is the only other supermarket with any market overlap.
</p><p>Kroger entered the competitive <a href="/wiki/San_Antonio,_Texas" class="mw-redirect" title="San Antonio, Texas">San Antonio, Texas</a>, market in 1980 but pulled out in mid-1993. On June 15, 1993, the company announced the closure of its 15 area stores.
</p><p>The chain closed several stores around <a href="/wiki/Flint,_Michigan" title="Flint, Michigan">Flint, Michigan</a>, in 1981, which were converted by local businessman Al Kessel to a new chain called <a href="/wiki/Kessel_Food_Markets" title="Kessel Food Markets">Kessel Food Markets</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Kroger bought most of these stores back in 1999 and began reverting them.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Several other Michigan stores were sold to another Flint-based chain, <a href="/wiki/Hamady_Brothers" title="Hamady Brothers">Hamady Brothers</a>, in 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> The Hamady acquisition was short-lived.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p><p>In 1982, Kroger sold the 65-store Market Basket chain it had operated for several years in southern California. The stores were reverted to the <a href="/wiki/Boys_Markets" class="mw-redirect" title="Boys Markets">Boys Markets</a> branding, after acquiring the chain. Boys Markets was acquired by the <a href="/wiki/Yucaipa_Companies" title="Yucaipa Companies">Yucaipa Companies</a> in 1989. When Yucaipa acquired <a href="/wiki/Ralphs" title="Ralphs">Ralphs</a>, the Boys brand disappeared.
</p><p>In 1983, The Kroger Company acquired <a href="/wiki/Dillons" title="Dillons">Dillon Companies</a><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> grocery chain in Kansas along with its subsidiaries (<a href="/wiki/King_Soopers" title="King Soopers">King Soopers</a>, <a href="/wiki/King_Soopers_%26_City_Market" class="mw-redirect" title="King Soopers &amp; City Market">City Market</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fry%27s_Food_and_Drug" title="Fry's Food and Drug">Fry's</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gerbes" class="mw-redirect" title="Gerbes">Gerbes</a>) and the convenience store chain <a href="/wiki/Kwik_Shop" title="Kwik Shop">Kwik Shop</a>. <a href="/wiki/David_Dillon" title="David Dillon">David Dillon</a>, a fourth-generation descendant of J. S. Dillon, the founder of Dillon Companies, became the CEO of Kroger.
</p><p>In northeastern Ohio, Kroger had a plant in <a href="/wiki/Solon,_Ohio" title="Solon, Ohio">Solon, Ohio</a> until the mid-1980s. When that plant shut down due to high local union labor costs,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Kroger closed its northeastern Ohio stores in the Cleveland, <a href="/wiki/Akron,_Ohio" title="Akron, Ohio">Akron</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Youngstown,_Ohio" title="Youngstown, Ohio">Youngstown</a> areas. Some of those former Kroger stores were taken over by stores like Acme Fresh Markets, <a href="/wiki/Giant_Eagle" title="Giant Eagle">Giant Eagle</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Heinens" class="mw-redirect" title="Heinens">Heinens</a>.
</p><p>Kroger opened and had about 50 stores in <a href="/wiki/St._Louis,_Missouri" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Louis, Missouri">St. Louis</a> until it left the market in 1986, saying that its stores were unprofitable. Most of its stores were bought by <a href="/wiki/National_Supermarkets" title="National Supermarkets">National</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schnucks" title="Schnucks">Schnucks</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shop_%27n_Save" title="Shop 'n Save">Shop 'n Save</a>.
</p><p>Kroger also experienced a similar withdrawal from <a href="/wiki/Chattanooga,_Tennessee" title="Chattanooga, Tennessee">Chattanooga, Tennessee</a>, in 1989. Many of these stores were sold to the local grocery chain <a href="/wiki/Red_Food" title="Red Food">Red Food</a>, which was in turn bought by <a href="/wiki/BI-LO_(United_States)" title="BI-LO (United States)">BI-LO</a> in 1994. Today, Chattanooga is the only metropolitan market in <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a> in which Kroger does not operate.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s">1990s</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kroger_in_Fort_Worth,_TX.png" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8e/Kroger_in_Fort_Worth%2C_TX.png/220px-Kroger_in_Fort_Worth%2C_TX.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="98" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1576" data-file-height="705"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 98px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8e/Kroger_in_Fort_Worth%2C_TX.png/220px-Kroger_in_Fort_Worth%2C_TX.png" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="98" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kroger_in_Fort_Worth,_TX.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A regional Kroger in <a href="/wiki/Fort_Worth,_Texas" title="Fort Worth, Texas">Fort Worth, Texas</a>, opened in 1997 (2014)</div></div></div>
<p>In the 1990s, Kroger acquired Great Scott (Detroit), <a href="/wiki/Pay_Less_Food_Markets" class="mw-redirect" title="Pay Less Food Markets">Pay Less Food Markets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Owen%27s_Market" title="Owen's Market">Owen's Market</a>, <a href="/wiki/JayC_Food_Stores" title="JayC Food Stores">JayC Food Stores</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hilander_Foods" title="Hilander Foods">Hilander Foods</a>. Additionally, the Houston market was strengthened when Kroger bought several stores from <a href="/wiki/AppleTree_Markets" title="AppleTree Markets">AppleTree Markets</a>, which were former <a href="/wiki/Safeway_Inc." title="Safeway Inc.">Safeway</a> stores in early 1994.
</p><p>In 1998, Kroger merged with the then fifth-largest grocery company <a href="/wiki/Fred_Meyer" title="Fred Meyer">Fred Meyer</a>, along with its subsidiaries, <a href="/wiki/Ralphs" title="Ralphs">Ralphs</a>, <a href="/wiki/QFC" title="QFC">QFC</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Smith%27s_Food_and_Drug" title="Smith's Food and Drug">Smith's</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p><p>In the late 1990s, it acquired many stores from <a href="/wiki/A%26P" class="mw-redirect" title="A&amp;P">A&amp;P</a> as it exited many markets in the South.
</p><p>Kroger also swapped all ten of its <a href="/wiki/Greensboro,_North_Carolina" title="Greensboro, North Carolina">Greensboro, North Carolina</a>-area stores in 1999 to <a href="/wiki/Matthews,_North_Carolina" title="Matthews, North Carolina">Matthews, North Carolina</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Harris_Teeter" title="Harris Teeter">Harris Teeter</a>, for 11 of that company's stores in central and western <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>. Kroger still maintains a North Carolina presence in the <a href="/wiki/Raleigh-Durham" class="mw-redirect" title="Raleigh-Durham">Raleigh-Durham</a> area. In the <a href="/wiki/Raleigh-Durham" class="mw-redirect" title="Raleigh-Durham">Raleigh-Durham</a> area, Kroger closed its North Raleigh store in the Wakefield Commons shopping center on July 9, 2011, because the location failed to meet sales expectations. After the closure, Kroger will operate 16 stores in the Triangle. Kroger had a store in <a href="/wiki/Greenville,_North_Carolina" title="Greenville, North Carolina">Greenville</a> from the 1980s until 2010 when it sold it to Harris Teeter.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> A store in <a href="/wiki/Wilson,_North_Carolina" title="Wilson, North Carolina">Wilson</a> opened in 2002 but closed two years later.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="2000s">2000s</span></h3>
<p>Long the dominant grocer in western Virginia, Kroger entered the <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_Virginia" title="Richmond, Virginia">Richmond, Virginia</a>, market in 2000, where it competes against market leaders <a href="/wiki/Martin%27s_Food_Stores" class="mw-redirect" title="Martin's Food Stores">Martin's</a> (including former Ukrop's stores) and <a href="/wiki/Food_Lion" title="Food Lion">Food Lion</a>. Kroger entered the market by purchasing <a href="/wiki/Hannaford_Bros._Co." class="mw-redirect" title="Hannaford Bros. Co.">Hannaford</a> stores that either already existed or were being built in Richmond. Hannaford purchases also included the competitive <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads" title="Hampton Roads">Hampton Roads</a> market, where it now competes with <a href="/wiki/Farm_Fresh_Food_%26_Pharmacy" title="Farm Fresh Food &amp; Pharmacy">Farm Fresh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harris_Teeter" title="Harris Teeter">Harris Teeter</a> (which is owned by Kroger), and <a href="/wiki/Food_Lion" title="Food Lion">Food Lion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The Hannaford locations in these markets were purchased from <a href="/wiki/Delhaize_Group" title="Delhaize Group">Delhaize</a> by Kroger as a condition of Delhaize's 2000 acquisition of the Hannaford chain, which had previously competed against Food Lion, also owned by Delhaize.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Walmart Supercenters are also major competitors in both markets, and the chain briefly competed against <a href="/wiki/Winn-Dixie" title="Winn-Dixie">Winn-Dixie</a>, which has now exited Virginia.
</p><p>In 2001, Kroger acquired <a href="/wiki/Baker%27s_Supermarkets" title="Baker's Supermarkets">Baker's Supermarkets</a> from Fleming Companies, Inc.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/Albertsons" title="Albertsons">Albertsons</a> exited the San Antonio and Houston markets in early 2002, selling many of the Houston stores to Kroger.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In 2004, Kroger bought most of the old Thriftway stores in <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati,_Ohio" class="mw-redirect" title="Cincinnati, Ohio">Cincinnati, Ohio</a>, when <a href="/wiki/Winn-Dixie" title="Winn-Dixie">Winn-Dixie</a> left the area. These stores were reopened as Kroger stores.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In 2007, Kroger acquired <a href="/wiki/Scott%27s_Food_%26_Pharmacy" title="Scott's Food &amp; Pharmacy">Scott's Food &amp; Pharmacy</a> from <a href="/wiki/SuperValu_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="SuperValu Inc.">SuperValu Inc.</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> and in the same year, also
acquired 20 former Michigan Farmer Jack locations from A&amp;P when A&amp;P exited the Michigan Market.
</p><p>In 2008, Kroger began a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Murray%27s_Cheese" title="Murray's Cheese">Murray's Cheese</a> of New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-Lippman_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lippman-33">[33]</a></sup> Murray's Cheese counters within Kroger stores sell a variety of artisanal cheese from all parts of the world.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="2010s">2010s</span></h3>
<p>On July 9, 2013, Kroger announced its acquisition of (the 212 stores of Charlotte-based) <a href="/wiki/Harris_Teeter" title="Harris Teeter">Harris Teeter</a> in a deal valued at $2.5 billion and that it will assume $100 million in the company's outstanding debt.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Harris Teeter's stores are in eight Southern states, with a major portion of them in its headquarters state of North Carolina.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Doing so, Kroger acquired Harris Teeter's click and collect program which allows online ordering of groceries. Some industry experts see this as a competitive move against <a href="/wiki/Online_grocer" title="Online grocer">online grocers</a> such as <a href="/wiki/AmazonFresh" title="AmazonFresh">AmazonFresh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup>  The Harris Teeter acquisition marked Kroger's return to the Charlotte market after a 25-year absence. It also allowed Kroger to enter <a href="/wiki/Asheville,_North_Carolina" title="Asheville, North Carolina">Asheville</a> for the first time. Charlotte and Asheville had been the only large markets in North Carolina where Kroger had no presence.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In 2013, Kroger announced that the spouses of the company's unionized workers would no longer be covered by the company's insurance plan. The company cited the <a href="/wiki/Patient_Protection_and_Affordable_Care_Act" title="Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act">Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act</a> as a prime reason for the move. The benefit cut affects roughly 11,000 workers in Indiana.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The company announced in April 2013 that full-time employees would maintain their health insurance benefits.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p><p>On March 3, 2015, Kroger announced it will enter <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>, having registered with the state as a new business in February 2015. The move had been in the planning stages, as it was planning to expand there in 2006 but withdrew after it had already submitted registration. Kroger, which is in the process of looking for locations to open its first store, will face competition from Honolulu-based rivals <a href="/wiki/Foodland_Hawaii" title="Foodland Hawaii">Foodland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Times_Supermarkets" title="Times Supermarkets">Times</a>; major retailers Safeway, Walmart, and <a href="/wiki/Costco" title="Costco">Costco</a>; Japanese-owned Don Quixote; and Department of Defense-owned DeCA Commissaries.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p><p>On May 1, 2015, Kroger announced the acquisition of the seven-store Hiller's Market chain in Southeast Michigan, and that it would operate all but one of those stores under the Kroger banner.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p><p>In June 2015, Kroger eliminated the Harris Teeter brand from the crowded Nashville, Tennessee market, where its growth had been stunted by aggressive competition since it entered with six stores in the early-2000s.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Kroger has traditionally had a market-leading presence in Nashville, and initially promised to keep the five remaining Harris Teeter stores open when it acquired the chain,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> but later said the market "did not support Harris Teeter's future business plans."<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Two Harris Teeter stores were closed outright, and three closed temporarily while being converted to the Kroger brand (one of these would undergo a major remodeling and replace a neighboring Kroger store).<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p><p>On November 11, 2015, Kroger and <a href="/wiki/Roundy%27s" title="Roundy's">Roundy's</a> announced a definitive merger, bringing Roundy's chain's 166 primarily Wisconsin based chains under Kroger ownership. The merger is valued at $800 million, including debt. The acquisition, which brought Kroger back to Wisconsin after a 43-year absence, will retain the Roundy's, Pick 'n Save, Mariano's, Metro Market and Copps names, along with its Milwaukee operations.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p><p>In April 2016, Kroger announced that it had made a "meaningful investment" in the <a href="/wiki/Boulder,_Colorado" title="Boulder, Colorado">Boulder, Colorado</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Lucky%27s_Market" title="Lucky's Market">Lucky's Market</a>, an organic foods supermarket chain that operated 17 stores in 13 states throughout the Midwest and Southeast United States.<sup id="cite_ref-prn-2016apr01_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prn-2016apr01-47">[47]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2017, Kroger withstood large community protests after announcing the closing of two smaller-sized Louisville-area stores.
Despite high store volumes and high population densities, the Old Louisville (lease expiration) and Southland Terrace stores closed.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p><p>On February 7, 2017 it was announced that Kroger Co. had purchased Murray's Cheese.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p><p>As of 14 February 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kroger&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Kroger is no longer offering a discount to senior citizens 59 and up.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p><p>On May 1, 2017, Kroger, along with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky" title="University of Kentucky">University of Kentucky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Wildcats" title="Kentucky Wildcats">UK Athletics</a>, sports and campus marketing partner JMI Sports, announced a 12-year, $1.85 million per year campus marketing agreement. Included in the agreement is the <a href="/wiki/Naming_rights" title="Naming rights">naming rights</a> to Commonwealth Stadium, the university's <a href="/wiki/Gridiron_football" title="Gridiron football">football</a> stadium, which will be renamed <a href="/wiki/Kroger_Field" title="Kroger Field">Kroger Field</a>. This agreement makes the University of Kentucky the first school in the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference" title="Southeastern Conference">Southeastern Conference</a> to enter into a corporate partnership for the naming rights to their football stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-HL20170501_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HL20170501-51">[51]</a></sup></p><p>On May 10, 2017, Kroger opened its first convenience store<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Blacklick,_Ohio" title="Blacklick, Ohio">Blacklick, Ohio</a>, labeled "Fresh Eats MKT". The new <a href="/wiki/Prototype" title="Prototype">prototype stores</a> will have about 12,000 square feet of space, and will be very similar to the <a href="/wiki/Walmart_Neighborhood_Market" class="mw-redirect" title="Walmart Neighborhood Market">Walmart Neighborhood Market</a> project, as these stores only sell food. These stores have a <a href="/wiki/Starbucks" title="Starbucks">Starbucks</a>, and a Kroger Pharmacy. On June 1, 2017, Kroger opened their second Fresh Eats. Kroger is also going to convert some <a href="/wiki/Turkey_Hill_(company)" title="Turkey Hill (company)">Turkey Hill</a> stores into the concept store. The <a href="/wiki/Chief_financial_officer" title="Chief financial officer">CFO</a>, Mike Schlotman, has called these stores a "small test." Local reaction to this new concept has been positive.
</p><p>In February 2018, Kroger announced that it will be selling its 762 convenience stores to <a href="/wiki/EG_Group" title="EG Group">EG Group</a>, a British gas station operator, for $2.15 billion. They operate under the <i>Turkey Hill</i>, <i>Loaf 'N Jug</i>, <i>Kwik Shop</i>, <i>Tom Thumb</i> and <i>Quik Stop</i> banners. Kroger will retain just over 20 convenience stores.  Kroger's supermarket fuel centers are not included in the sale.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> The sale was closed on April 20, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p><p>On April 10, 2018, Kroger announced plans to hire an estimated 11,000 new employees. An estimated 2,000 managerial positions will be filled by the new hires. With the addition of these new hires, the total number of people employed by the company is close to half a million.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p><p>On May 17, 2018, Kroger announced a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Ocado" title="Ocado">Ocado</a>, a UK-based online supermarket. The partnership is designed to improve Kroger's ecommerce program, including online ordering, automated fulfillment, and home delivery via the construction of 20 new, automated fulfillment centers. <sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> As of November 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kroger&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, five locations have been identified for the new warehouses, and two are under construction.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p><p>On May 24, 2018, Kroger announced they were acquiring <a href="/wiki/Home_Chef" title="Home Chef">Home Chef</a> for $200 million with an additional $500 million in incentives if certain targets are met by Home Chef.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>On June 13, 2018, Kroger Mid-Atlantic announced that they will be leaving the Raleigh-Durham area by closing and selling all 14 of their stores, 8 of which will become Harris Teeter stores. One will become a Crunch Fitness and another will become a Food Lion. The fate for the remaining 4 stores is unclear.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p><p>In July 2018, Kroger officials backed off a <a href="/wiki/Net_D" title="Net D">Net 90</a> payment plan to the produce industry.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2018, Kroger announced online wine delivery to 14 states in partnership with DRINKS.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Customers can select assorted wines in 6-bottle or 12-bottle packs. <sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p><p>On December 4, 2018, Kroger announced a deal to sell food inside drugstore <a href="/wiki/Walgreens" title="Walgreens">Walgreens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Kroger Express<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> will offer meal kits and other meal solutions.
</p><p>In the light of increased self-checkout usage via kiosk or smartphone app in 2019, Kroger is gradually shifting towards creating more self-checkout smartphone apps and lanes than cashier lanes. The company has been investing millions of dollars, in replacing many cashier stations with automation by 2023. As many other supermarkets (such as <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Target_Corporation" title="Target Corporation">Target</a>, etc.) are also shifting towards automation, and displacing cashiers in the near future.<sup id="cite_ref-Waco_Tribune-Herald_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Waco_Tribune-Herald-67">[67]</a></sup></p><p>In March 2019, Kroger announced it was expanding its service with robotics company, <a href="/wiki/Nuro" title="Nuro">Nuro</a> to Houston, Texas with Nuro's autonomous Priuses.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p><p>In August 2019, Kroger began charging customers between $0.50 and $3.50 for receiving cash back while making purchases with debit cards.<sup id="cite_ref-ce-2019jul30_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ce-2019jul30-69">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-retailwire-2019jul31_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-retailwire-2019jul31-70">[70]</a></sup> The new fees were first test marketed in March at Kansas area <a href="/wiki/Dillons" title="Dillons">Dillons</a> stores, a Kroger-owned supermarket chain, before the new fees were rolled out to other Kroger-owned supermarket banners in the rest of the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-we-2019mar04_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-we-2019mar04-71">[71]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2019, Kroger announced a partnership with the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://plantbasedfoods.org/">Plant Based Food Association</a> (PFBA) to test a plant-based meat retail concept in 60 stores in Denver, and parts of Indiana and Illinois.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p><p>In November 2019, Kroger unveiled an updated logo for their stores and company, removing the blue circle that the logo had previously resided in.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The company also announced an expansion of its online wine delivery program into Arizona.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> In partnership with DRINKS, the service is now available in 19 states plus Washington D.C.. <sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p><p>In December 2019, Kroger was named the second-largest grocer in the nation with $110 billion dollars in 2016 sales. The same month, <i>USA Today</i> listed Kroger -- and its brands -- as the top supermarket (based on Google searches, Yelp data and 24/7 Tempo's research) in Alaska, Indiana, Kentucky, Mississippi, Ohio, Oregon, Tennessee, Virginia, Washington, and West Virginia. <sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">Finances</span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<p>For the fiscal year 2017, Kroger reported earnings of US$1.907 billion, with an annual revenue of US$122.662 billion, an increase of 6.4% over the previous fiscal cycle. Kroger's shares traded at over $142 per share, and its market capitalization was valued at US$24 billion in October 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
