<td><small>Convenience</small>
</td></tr></tbody></table></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Kroger_Marketplace">Kroger Marketplace</span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<p><b>Kroger Marketplace</b> is a chain of <a href="/wiki/Big-box_store" title="Big-box store">big-box stores</a>. The brand was introduced in 2004 in the <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio" title="Columbus, Ohio">Columbus, Ohio</a>, area, which lost the <a href="/wiki/Big_Bear_Stores" title="Big Bear Stores">Big Bear</a> and Big Bear Plus chains in <a href="/wiki/Penn_Traffic" title="Penn Traffic">Penn Traffic</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Chapter_11,_Title_11,_United_States_Code" title="Chapter 11, Title 11, United States Code">Chapter 11 bankruptcy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> The Kroger Marketplace format is based on the <a href="/wiki/Fry%27s_Food_and_Drug#Fry's_Marketplace" title="Fry's Food and Drug">Fry's Marketplace</a> stores that the Arizona division of Kroger is currently operating. There are currently a total of 183 marketplaces.<sup id="cite_ref-ourbusiness_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ourbusiness-1">[1]</a></sup></p><p>Similar to rival chains <a href="/wiki/Meijer" title="Meijer">Meijer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sears" title="Sears">Sears</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kmart" title="Kmart">Kmart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Target_Corporation" title="Target Corporation">Target</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Albertsons" title="Albertsons">Albertsons</a>, and modeled after Kroger-owned Fred Meyer, these stores contain multiple departments.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> In addition to the grocery department, they usually contain a <a href="/wiki/Fred_Meyer_Jewelers" title="Fred Meyer Jewelers">Fred Meyer Jewelers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Starbucks" title="Starbucks">Starbucks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Donatos_Pizza" title="Donatos Pizza">Donatos Pizza</a>, and an in-store bank, as well as sections for toys, appliances, home furnishings and bed and bath, something that Big Bear once had in their stores in the Columbus area.
</p><p>In 2005, the company began renovating many <i>Kroger Food &amp; Drug</i> stores in Ohio for an expanded and remodeled look, converting them to the <i>Kroger Marketplace</i> format. In February 2006, Kroger announced plans for two new Kroger Marketplace stores to open by the end of the summer in Cincinnati suburbs <a href="/wiki/Lebanon,_Ohio" title="Lebanon, Ohio">Lebanon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Township,_Butler_County,_Ohio" title="Liberty Township, Butler County, Ohio">Liberty Township</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-note1_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-note1-98">[98]</a></sup> The store in Liberty Township opened in July 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-note2_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-note2-99">[99]</a></sup> On October 5, 2006, a new Kroger Marketplace opened in <a href="/wiki/Gahanna,_Ohio" title="Gahanna, Ohio">Gahanna</a>. With the Gahanna opening, the number of Kroger Marketplace stores is six, four in the Columbus area and two in the Cincinnati area. Two more stores were planned in 2007, one in Middletown (which opened in April 2007, after the old store was razed and made part of the current parking lot) and one in Englewood.<sup id="cite_ref-note3_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-note3-100">[100]</a></sup></p><p>In 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Elder-Beerman" title="Elder-Beerman">Elder-Beerman</a> in <a href="/wiki/Centerville,_Ohio" title="Centerville, Ohio">Centerville, Ohio</a> was demolished, and a new marketplace has been built in its place. It has a fuel center and opened on December 8.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> This marketplace is the largest Kroger store ever built from ground up to date at 147,000 square feet.
</p><p>Two more stores opened in the Cincinnati area, in the Northern Kentucky suburbs of <a href="/wiki/Hebron,_Kentucky" title="Hebron, Kentucky">Hebron</a> and <a href="/wiki/Walton,_Kentucky" title="Walton, Kentucky">Walton</a> which were completed in November 2008. Three Kroger Marketplace stores in <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a> opened in 2009, two in <a href="/wiki/Lexington,_Kentucky" title="Lexington, Kentucky">Lexington</a> and one in <a href="/wiki/Newport,_Kentucky" title="Newport, Kentucky">Newport</a>. Another Marketplace opened in <a href="/wiki/Beavercreek,_Ohio" title="Beavercreek, Ohio">Beavercreek, Ohio</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Mount_Orab,_Ohio" title="Mount Orab, Ohio">Mount Orab, Ohio</a>, store opened in the spring of 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Kroger opened a new 60,000 sq ft (5,600 m<sup>2</sup>) store in <a href="/wiki/North_Augusta,_South_Carolina" title="North Augusta, South Carolina">North Augusta, South Carolina</a>. In 2015, a 145,000 square foot Marketplace was opened in the Cincinnati suburb of <a href="/wiki/Oakley,_Cincinnati" title="Oakley, Cincinnati">Oakley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kroger_Frisco.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Kroger_Frisco.jpg/220px-Kroger_Frisco.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1952"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 132px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Kroger_Frisco.jpg/220px-Kroger_Frisco.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="132" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kroger_Frisco.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kroger Marketplace in <a href="/wiki/Frisco,_Texas" title="Frisco, Texas">Frisco, Texas</a> opened in 2010.</div></div></div>
<p>The first Kroger Marketplace store in Texas opened on October 9, 2009, in the Waterside Marketplace in <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_Texas" title="Richmond, Texas">Richmond, Texas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> The second Kroger Marketplace store in <a href="/wiki/Rosenberg,_Texas" title="Rosenberg, Texas">Rosenberg, Texas</a>, opened on December 4, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> The third opened in <a href="/wiki/Frisco,_Texas" title="Frisco, Texas">Frisco, Texas</a>, in early 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-wfaa.com_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wfaa.com-106">[106]</a></sup> The fourth, in <a href="/wiki/Willis,_Texas" title="Willis, Texas">Willis, Texas</a>, opened on August 11, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Other Kroger Marketplace stores in Texas are in <a href="/wiki/Little_Elm,_Texas" title="Little Elm, Texas">Little Elm, Texas</a>; Fort Worth's Alliance Town Center; Mansfield;<sup id="cite_ref-wfaa.com_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wfaa.com-106">[106]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wylie,_Texas" title="Wylie, Texas">Wylie, Texas</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-Wylie_Living_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wylie_Living-108">[108]</a></sup> and Baytown, Texas.
</p><p>The first Kroger Marketplace store in Tennessee opened in <a href="/wiki/Farragut,_Tennessee" title="Farragut, Tennessee">Farragut, Tennessee</a> (a small suburb near <a href="/wiki/Knoxville,_Tennessee" title="Knoxville, Tennessee">Knoxville</a>) at the end of 2008, and a second store in <a href="/wiki/Thompson%27s_Station,_Tennessee" title="Thompson's Station, Tennessee">Thompson's Station, Tennessee</a>, about 20 miles (32 km) south of <a href="/wiki/Nashville" class="mw-redirect" title="Nashville">Nashville</a>, opened in early 2009. A third location opened in <a href="/wiki/Gallatin,_Tennessee" title="Gallatin, Tennessee">Gallatin, Tennessee</a>, on March 11, 2010.
</p><p>The first Kroger Marketplace in Arkansas opened in August 2010 on Chenal Parkway in <a href="/wiki/Little_Rock,_Arkansas" title="Little Rock, Arkansas">Little Rock, Arkansas</a>. Locations also opened in 2012 in <a href="/wiki/Conway,_Arkansas" title="Conway, Arkansas">Conway, Arkansas</a> and 2014 in <a href="/wiki/Jonesboro,_Arkansas" title="Jonesboro, Arkansas">Jonesboro, Arkansas</a>.
</p><p>The first Kroger Marketplace in Virginia opened on <a href="/wiki/Midlothian_Turnpike" class="mw-redirect" title="Midlothian Turnpike">Midlothian Turnpike</a> in <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_Virginia" title="Richmond, Virginia">Richmond, Virginia</a>, on the site of the former <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cloverleaf_Mall&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cloverleaf Mall (page does not exist)">Cloverleaf Mall</a> on December 6, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> Another Marketplace opened in <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach,_Virginia" title="Virginia Beach, Virginia">Virginia Beach, Virginia</a>, at the site of a former <a href="/wiki/Kmart" title="Kmart">Super Kmart</a>, on July 31, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup>  The third location opened in December 2013 in the Staples Mill shopping Center in <a href="/wiki/Henrico_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Henrico County">Henrico County</a>.  A fourth location opened on October 15, 2014, in <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_Virginia" title="Portsmouth, Virginia">Portsmouth, Virginia</a>, at the site of the former <a href="/wiki/I.C._Norcom_High_School" class="mw-redirect" title="I.C. Norcom High School">I.C. Norcom High School</a>.
</p><p>The first Kroger Marketplace in Mississippi opened on September 16, 2016 in Hernando to much fanfare. This store was formally a Kroger Food &amp; Drug with twelve aisles, now rebuilt with sixty-four, in addition to having a Starbucks, ClickList, and expanded deli inside.
</p><p>The first Kroger Marketplace in Indiana opened on September 29, 2011, on Dupont Road on Fort Wayne's northwest side. This store is a rebuilt Kroger Food &amp; Drug. A second Kroger Marketplace opened on October 4, 2012, from a rebuilt Scott's Food and Pharmacy in the Village at Coventry on the southwest side of Fort Wayne. These two stores are part of a $100 million expansion project in the Fort Wayne area. In October 2016, it was announced that a Kroger Marketplace will open in <a href="/wiki/La_Porte,_Indiana" title="La Porte, Indiana">La Porte, Indiana</a> within the NewPorte Landing development. Construction of the new 123,000 square foot store is expected to begin early in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p><p>The first Kroger Marketplace in Michigan opened on June 14, 2013, at Sterns and Secor Roads in <a href="/wiki/Lambertville,_Michigan" title="Lambertville, Michigan">Lambertville</a> (a small-sized suburb north of <a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Ohio" title="Toledo, Ohio">Toledo, Ohio</a>). Formerly a conventional Kroger store, the square footage increased from 68,000 to 133,000 square feet. It carries toys, home essentials, apparel and shoes in addition to groceries. The state's second store opened in 2014 in <a href="/wiki/Shelby_Charter_Township,_Michigan" title="Shelby Charter Township, Michigan">Shelby Township</a> on property that already contained a 2010-built Fuel Center, replacing a smaller Kroger store across Hayes Road in neighboring <a href="/wiki/Macomb_Township,_Michigan" title="Macomb Township, Michigan">Macomb Township</a>, which was soon converted into an <a href="/wiki/Emagine_Entertainment" title="Emagine Entertainment">Emagine Entertainment</a> <a href="/wiki/Movie_theater" title="Movie theater">movie theater</a>.  Three further locations opened in 2016, one in <a href="/wiki/White_Lake_Township,_Michigan" title="White Lake Township, Michigan">White Lake</a> on the site of what was once one of Kmart's "green" prototype stores and directly adjacent to the smaller Kroger store that this location replaced, a second Shelby Township location at 26 Mile Road and Van Dyke Avenue, and one at 12 Mile Road and Stephenson Highway in <a href="/wiki/Royal_Oak,_Michigan" title="Royal Oak, Michigan">Royal Oak</a>. A sixth location opened on Fort Street in <a href="/wiki/Southgate,_Michigan" title="Southgate, Michigan">Southgate</a> on September 20, 2017. This store, which is a former Super Kmart, is the largest Kroger location in Michigan,<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> with seventy aisles along with a small cafe section and dedicated ClickList parking spaces.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Manufacturing_and_distribution">Manufacturing and distribution</span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Distribution_and_logistics">Distribution and logistics</span></h3>
<p>Food distribution and buying takes place under various subsidiaries and divisions. These include:<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li>Kroger Group Cooperative, Inc.</li>
<li>Kroger Group, Inc.</li>
<li>Peytons</li>
<li>WESCO</li>
<li>Inter-American Products</li></ul><p>Kroger operates its own fleet of trucks and trailers to distribute products to its various stores, in addition to contracts with various trucking companies.<sup id="cite_ref-proxystatement_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-proxystatement-2">[2]</a></sup> In June 2018, Kroger announced testing <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_car" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous car">driverless cars</a> for delivering groceries. For this, Kroger is partnering with autonomous car company <a href="/wiki/Nuro" title="Nuro">Nuro</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p><p>In addition to stocking a variety of regional brand products, The Kroger Company also employs one of the largest networks of private label manufacturing in the country. Thirty-seven plants (either wholly owned or used with operating agreements) in seventeen states create about 40% of Kroger's private label products.<sup id="cite_ref-proxystatement_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-proxystatement-2">[2]</a></sup> Similar to most major supermarket retailers, Kroger uses a three-tiered <a href="/wiki/Private_label" title="Private label">private label</a> marketing strategy. One private brand emphasizes no-frills products at the lowest possible price, another is intended to be comparable to leading national brands but a better value and the third is a premium (often organic) brand.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Manufacturing_plants">Manufacturing plants</span></h3>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Dairies">Dairies</span></h4>
<p>Kroger operates 18 dairy plants:
</p>
<ul><li>Centennial Farms Dairy – <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta, Georgia</a></li>
<li>Compton Creamery – <a href="/wiki/Compton,_California" title="Compton, California">Compton, California</a></li>
<li>Crossroad Farms Dairy – <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis" title="Indianapolis">Indianapolis, Indiana</a></li>
<li>Heritage Farms Dairy – <a href="/wiki/Murfreesboro,_Tennessee" title="Murfreesboro, Tennessee">Murfreesboro, Tennessee</a></li>
<li>Hunter Farms Dairy – <a href="/wiki/High_Point,_North_Carolina" title="High Point, North Carolina">High Point, North Carolina</a></li>
<li>Jackson Hutchinson Dairy – <a href="/wiki/Hutchinson,_Kansas" title="Hutchinson, Kansas">Hutchinson, Kansas</a></li>
<li>Layton Dairy – <a href="/wiki/Layton,_Utah" title="Layton, Utah">Layton, Utah</a></li>
<li>Michigan Dairy – <a href="/wiki/Livonia,_Michigan" title="Livonia, Michigan">Livonia, Michigan</a></li>
<li>Mountain View Foods – <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver, Colorado</a></li>
<li>Pace Dairy – Rochester - <a href="/wiki/Rochester,_Minnesota" title="Rochester, Minnesota">Rochester, Minnesota</a></li>
<li>Pace Dairy - Indiana – <a href="/wiki/Crawfordsville,_Indiana" title="Crawfordsville, Indiana">Crawfordsville, Indiana</a></li>
<li>Riverside Creamery – <a href="/wiki/Riverside,_California" title="Riverside, California">Riverside, California</a></li>
<li>Swan Island Dairy – <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon" title="Portland, Oregon">Portland, Oregon</a></li>
<li>Tamarack Farms Dairy – <a href="/wiki/Newark,_Ohio" title="Newark, Ohio">Newark, Ohio</a></li>
<li>Tolleson Dairy – <a href="/wiki/Tolleson,_Arizona" title="Tolleson, Arizona">Tolleson, Arizona</a></li>
<li>Vandervoort's Dairy – <a href="/wiki/Fort_Worth,_Texas" title="Fort Worth, Texas">Fort Worth, Texas</a></li>
<li>Westover Dairy – <a href="/wiki/Lynchburg,_Virginia" title="Lynchburg, Virginia">Lynchburg, Virginia</a></li>
<li>Winchester Farms Dairy – <a href="/wiki/Winchester,_Kentucky" title="Winchester, Kentucky">Winchester, Kentucky</a></li></ul><h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Bakeries">Bakeries</span></h4>
<p>Kroger operates 9 plants:
</p>
<ul><li>Anderson Bakery – <a href="/wiki/Anderson,_South_Carolina" title="Anderson, South Carolina">Anderson, South Carolina</a></li>
<li>Clackamas Bakery – <a href="/wiki/Clackamas,_Oregon" title="Clackamas, Oregon">Clackamas, Oregon</a></li>
<li>Country Oven Bakery – <a href="/wiki/Bowling_Green,_Kentucky" title="Bowling Green, Kentucky">Bowling Green, Kentucky</a></li>
<li>Indianapolis Bakery – <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis" title="Indianapolis">Indianapolis, Indiana</a></li>
<li>K.B. Specialty Foods – <a href="/wiki/Greensburg,_Indiana" title="Greensburg, Indiana">Greensburg, Indiana</a></li>
<li>King Soopers Bakery – <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver, Colorado</a></li>
<li>La Habra Bakery – <a href="/wiki/La_Habra,_California" title="La Habra, California">La Habra, California</a></li>
<li>Layton Dough – <a href="/wiki/Layton,_Utah" title="Layton, Utah">Layton, Utah</a></li>
<li>RCK Foods – <a href="/wiki/Kenosha,_Wisconsin" title="Kenosha, Wisconsin">Kenosha, Wisconsin</a></li></ul><h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Grocery_items">Grocery items</span></h4>
<p>Kroger operates 7 grocery plants:
</p>
<ul><li>America's Beverage Co. – <a href="/wiki/Irving,_Texas" title="Irving, Texas">Irving, Texas</a> – soft drinks, waters</li>
<li>Delight Products – <a href="/wiki/Springfield,_Tennessee" title="Springfield, Tennessee">Springfield, Tennessee</a> – dry dog and cat foods</li>
<li>Kenlake Foods – <a href="/wiki/Murray,_Kentucky" title="Murray, Kentucky">Murray, Kentucky</a> – nuts, hot cereal, cornmeal, powdered drinks</li>
<li>Pontiac Foods – <a href="/wiki/Pontiac,_South_Carolina" title="Pontiac, South Carolina">Pontiac, South Carolina</a> – coffee, seasonings, spices, rice, noodles, sauces</li>
<li>Springdale Ice Cream &amp; Beverage – <a href="/wiki/Springdale,_Ohio" title="Springdale, Ohio">Springdale, Ohio</a> – soft drinks, waters, ice cream</li>
<li>State Avenue – <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati,_Ohio" class="mw-redirect" title="Cincinnati, Ohio">Cincinnati, Ohio</a> – salad dressings, red sauces, syrups, broths, jams and jellies</li>
<li>Tara Foods – <a href="/wiki/Albany,_Georgia" title="Albany, Georgia">Albany, Georgia</a> – peanut butter, flavorings, steak sauces, vinegar, cooking wines, lemon juice, soy sauce<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Private_label_brands">Private label brands</span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<p>Kroger offers a collection of its own branded products, referred to by the retailer as "Our Brands". The products are produced and sold in quality tiers, and account for over 30% of the retailer's unit sales.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Banner_Brand">Banner Brand</span></h3>
<p>Banner Brand items are goods that bear the name of Kroger or its subsidiaries (i.e., Ralphs, King Soopers, etc.) or make reference to them (i.e., Big K), and are offered exclusively within Kroger-owned stores. These products are marketed to customers as budget-friendly, and account for over $13 billion in annual sales.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> Many of Kroger's health and beauty goods, one of the company's fastest-growing private label categories, are manufactured by third-party providers; these products include goods like <a href="/wiki/Ibuprofen" title="Ibuprofen">ibuprofen</a> and contact lens solution.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Private_Selection">Private Selection</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r923042769/mw-parser-output/.tmulti"><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:154px;max-width:154px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:KrogerPrivateSelection.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/KrogerPrivateSelection.jpg/150px-KrogerPrivateSelection.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="49" data-file-width="549" data-file-height="181"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 150px;height: 49px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/KrogerPrivateSelection.jpg/150px-KrogerPrivateSelection.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="150" data-height="49"> </span></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">Private Selection branding</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Simple_Truth_logo.png" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/df/Simple_Truth_logo.png/150px-Simple_Truth_logo.png" decoding="async" width="150" height="155" data-file-width="310" data-file-height="320"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 150px;height: 155px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/df/Simple_Truth_logo.png/150px-Simple_Truth_logo.png" data-alt="" data-width="150" data-height="155"> </span></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">Simple Truth logo</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Products marked <i>Private Selection</i> are offered to compare with gourmet brands or regional brands that may be considered more upscale than the standard Kroger brand products.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Simple_Truth">Simple Truth</span></h3>
<p><i>Simple Truth</i> is Kroger's flagship natural and organic brand, and has grown quickly since its launch in 2012. The brand's launch marked the first time Kroger had delved into making its own gluten-free products, including flour mixes, bread, etc. The Simple Truth brand became the first Kroger offering to be introduced in China, on <a href="/wiki/Alibaba_Group" title="Alibaba Group">Alibaba's</a> <a href="/wiki/Tmall" title="Tmall">Tmall</a> platform.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Simple Truth reached $2 billion in annual sales in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_private_label_brands">Other private label brands</span></h3>
<p>In addition to its core brands, Kroger's manufacturing creates a variety department-specific brands. These are featured especially in Fred Meyer stores, where more than half the goods sold are non-food, or in the smaller Fred Meyer-based Marketplace stores. The brands listed below may be found in various Kroger-owned stores.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li><b>Abound</b> – natural pet food</li>
<li><b>Bakery Fresh Goodness</b> – fresh-baked foods</li>
<li><b>Bloom Haus</b> – floral arrangements</li>
<li><b>Comforts</b> – baby products</li>
<li><b>Dip</b> – <a href="/wiki/Fast_fashion" title="Fast fashion">fast fashion</a> brand designed by <a href="/wiki/Joe_Mimran" title="Joe Mimran">Joe Mimran</a><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Everyday Living</b> – home goods</li>
<li><b>HD Designs</b> – upscale home goods</li>
<li><b>HemisFares</b> – imported foods</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Home_Chef" title="Home Chef">Home Chef</a></b> – meal kit and food delivery company acquired in 2018</li>
<li><b>Luvsome</b> – pet food</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Murray%27s_Cheese" title="Murray's Cheese">Murray's Cheese</a></b> – artisanal cheese shop founded in <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Village" title="Greenwich Village">Greenwich Village</a> in 1940</li>
<li><b>OfficeWorks</b> – stationery and office supplies</li>
<li><b>Pet Pride</b> – pet food</li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_operations">Other operations</span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Pharmacy_Group">Pharmacy Group</span></h3>
<p>Kroger previously owned and operated the <b>SupeRx</b> drug store chain. In 1985, Kroger outbid <a href="/wiki/Rite_Aid" title="Rite Aid">Rite Aid</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Hook%27s_Drug_Stores" title="Hook's Drug Stores">Hook's Drug Stores</a> chain, based in <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis" title="Indianapolis">Indianapolis</a>, Indiana, and combined it with SupeRx to become <b>Hook's-SupeRx</b>. In 1994, Kroger decided to exit the stand-alone drugstore business and sold its Hook's and SupeRx stores to <a href="/wiki/Revco" title="Revco">Revco</a>, which later was sold to <a href="/wiki/CVS_Caremark" title="CVS Caremark">CVS</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p><p>Today, Kroger operates 2,271 pharmacies, most of which are located inside its supermarkets.<sup id="cite_ref-ourbusiness_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ourbusiness-1">[1]</a></sup> The Kroger Pharmacies continue as a profitable portion of the business and have been expanding to now include pharmacies in City Market, Dillons, Fred Meyer, Fry's, King Soopers, QFC, Ralphs, Harris Teeter, Smith's Food and Drug, and Kroger Supermarkets.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Supermarket_Petroleum_Group">Supermarket Petroleum Group</span></h3>
<p>Since 1998, Kroger has added fuel centers in the parking lots of its supermarkets. More recently, the company has begun opening standalone fuel centers, often near stores whose parking lots could not accommodate a fuel center. As of Q2 2018, Kroger operated 1,523 supermarket fuel centers.<sup id="cite_ref-ourbusiness_1-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ourbusiness-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-opera_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opera-7">[7]</a></sup></p><p>In 2006, Kroger introduced a new common <a href="/wiki/Logo" title="Logo">logo</a> for all of its convenience store chains that is now also used at the fuel centers of all of its supermarket chains—a <a href="/wiki/Rhombus" title="Rhombus">rhombus</a> with a white, <a href="/wiki/Stylized_art" class="mw-redirect" title="Stylized art">stylized image</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Continental_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Continental United States">continental United States</a> in the center bordered by four colored areas: dark blue representing the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>, red representing <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, green representing the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, and yellow representing the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Kroger_Personal_Finance">Kroger Personal Finance</span></h3>
<p>Kroger Personal Finance was introduced in 2007 to offer branded Visa cards; mortgages; home equity loans; pet, renter's and home insurance; identity theft protection; and wireless services.<sup id="cite_ref-proxystatement_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-proxystatement-2">[2]</a></sup> In 2011, Kroger dropped its contract with MasterCard and now offers store credit and debit cards through Visa.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Kroger_Wireless">Kroger Wireless</span></h3>
<p>Kroger Wireless, formerly known as <a href="/wiki/I-wireless" title="I-wireless">i-wireless</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> is a national private label wireless service provider sold in over 2,200 retail locations within the Kroger family of stores across 31 states.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-128">[128]</a></sup>  Kroger Wireless service functions over the nationwide <a href="/wiki/Sprint_Corporation" title="Sprint Corporation">Sprint</a> network.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> Customers can choose from “Unlimited” rate plans including unlimited talk/<a href="/wiki/Text_messaging" title="Text messaging">text</a> and with data allotments up to and including unlimited data.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> Kroger Wireless allows customers to purchase phones at select Kroger store locations,<sup id="cite_ref-:0_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-128">[128]</a></sup> via their website,<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> or by bringing their eligible Sprint device for activation.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="84.51.C2.B0"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="84.51°">84.51°</span></h3>
<p>84.51° is a wholly owned subsidiary of Kroger engaged in data analytics and consumer insights, created in April 2015, as a result of <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Kroger</a> purchasing most of Dunnhumby USA.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">
<p>In 2008, <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace" title="Greenpeace">Greenpeace</a> started ranking America's major supermarket chains on their seafood sustainability practices because, according to <a href="/wiki/Phil_Radford" title="Phil Radford">Phil Radford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace" title="Greenpeace">Greenpeace</a> U.S. CEO, "three quarters of global fish stocks are suffering from overfishing,<sup id="cite_ref-United_Nations_Food_and_Agriculture_Organization_(FAO)_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-United_Nations_Food_and_Agriculture_Organization_(FAO)-134">[134]</a></sup> and 90% of top marine predators are already gone."<sup id="cite_ref-University_of_British_Columbia_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-University_of_British_Columbia-135">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Seek_Radio_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Seek_Radio-136">[136]</a></sup> Criteria included the number of threatened fish species supermarkets sold, their seafood purchasing policies, and ocean legislation policies they supported.<sup id="cite_ref-Greenbiz.com_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greenbiz.com-137">[137]</a></sup> In 2013, Kroger was noted for carrying 17 out of 22 red list<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (October 2017)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> species, four of which are top-tier red list species.<sup id="cite_ref-Greenpeace_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greenpeace-138">[138]</a></sup></p><p>In 2014, <a href="/wiki/Moms_Demand_Action_for_Gun_Sense_in_America" class="mw-redirect" title="Moms Demand Action for Gun Sense in America">Moms Demand Action for Gun Sense in America</a>, a national gun control organization backed by former New York Mayor Michael Bloomberg, began a campaign that seeks to pressure the Kroger chain to ban the open carry of firearms in all of its stores. The group decided to take action in response to demonstrations by open carry activists in Kroger stores in Ohio and Texas, and after conducting research that identified more than a dozen shootings on Kroger property since 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Kroger_Under_Fire_From_Gun-Control_Moms_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kroger_Under_Fire_From_Gun-Control_Moms-139">[139]</a></sup> Kroger rebuffed their demand, stating, "If the local gun laws are to allow open carry, we'll certainly allow customers to do that based on what the local laws are. We don't believe it's up to us to legislate what the local gun control laws should be. It's up to the local legislators to decide to do that. So we follow local laws, we ask our customers to be respectful to the other people they are shopping with. And we really haven't had any issues inside of our stores as a result of that."<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(9)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span></h2><section class="mf-section-9 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-9">
